## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and current concentration. The rate law typically depends on powers of concentration, and time-dependence may arise from external forcing, competing pathways, or catalyst deactivation.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Competing reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturating kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Time-dependent decay with reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation or time-varying rate)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (generalized rate with source/sink term)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Combined time and concentration: dA_dt = c0 * A * t**c1 (power-law time dependence in rate)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)
- Two-term rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic polynomial in concentration)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration power-law dependence → dA/dt ~ A^n indicates reaction order n, which reflects molecularity of the elementary step
- Negative rate constant sign → indicates consumption/decay of species A (reactant being consumed)
- Rational dependence on A (Michaelis-Menten form) → suggests enzyme catalysis or surface adsorption limiting step
- Product of A and (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic growth behavior where both reactant and product participate
- Explicit time dependence in rate → suggests non-autonomous system such as photolysis, temperature ramping, or catalyst deactivation
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → indicates parallel reaction pathways with different orders
- Hill-type sigmoidal dependence on A → cooperative binding or allosteric enzyme regulation
- Rate expression with A in denominator → product inhibition or competitive inhibition mechanism
- Exponential dependence on t multiplied by A → time-varying rate coefficient, possibly from temperature programming (Arrhenius with T(t))
- Square root of A in rate law → half-order kinetics typical of chain reactions or surface-mediated dissociation
